  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b00e2004-20ad-4e71-838f-15facad440aa'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<a href="/questions/1077455-i-ve-read-the-first-book-in-the-adversary">I&#39;ve read the first book in the Adversary Cycle, how does this book continue from the The Keep? I liked The Keep but I am not sure I should read this one. Any recommendations?</a>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/76013932-clayton-v"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/76013932-clayton-v">Clayton V.</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">"The Tomb" and "The Touch" were made part of the Adversary Cycle when "Nightworld" was released. Originally "The Keep", "Reborn", & "Reprisal" were th<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">"The Tomb" and "The Touch" were made part of the Adversary Cycle when "Nightworld" was released. Originally "The Keep", "Reborn", &amp; "Reprisal" were the series and then, when "Nightworld" came out, characters from "The Tomb" and "The Touch" were rolled in to the same continuity. I recommend reading "The Tomb" after reading "Reborn" and "Reprisal" but before reading "Nightworld". That way you are familiar all the characters for the end of the series.<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_538341292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/538341292" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/538341292?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780765355133" href="/book/show/219407.The_Tomb_Adversary_Cycle_2_">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=acquired-in-2013">acquired-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer538341292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4684478014591198518"><br/><i>All she could do was stand there and scream.</i><br/><br/>Indeed. <br/><br/>This book has a good number of things going for it. I particularly enjoyed the characterization of Repairman Jack. There are also some Lovecraftian references that fans will recognize. <br/><br/><i>Striding down the dark passage like the avatar of a vengeful god, came Jack.</i><br/><br/>I can imagine that followers of the <i>Agent Pendergast</i> series (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/67035.Relic__Pendergast___1_' title='Relic (Pendergast, #1) by Douglas Preston' rel='nofollow noopener'>Relic</a>), the <i>Charlie Parker</i> series (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/175242.Every_Dead_Thing__Charlie_Parker___1_' title='Every Dead Thing (Charlie Parker, #1) by John Connolly' rel='nofollow noopener'>Every Dead Thing</a>) or the <i>Harry Dresden</i> series (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47212.Storm_Front__The_Dresden_Files___1_' title='Storm Front (The Dresden Files, #1) by Jim Butcher' rel='nofollow noopener'>Storm Front</a>) would enjoy this, especially co</span>
  <span id="freeText4684478014591198518" style="display:none"><br /><i>All she could do was stand there and scream.</i><br /><br />Indeed. <br /><br />This book has a good number of things going for it. I particularly enjoyed the characterization of Repairman Jack. There are also some Lovecraftian references that fans will recognize. <br /><br /><i>Striding down the dark passage like the avatar of a vengeful god, came Jack.</i><br /><br />I can imagine that followers of the <i>Agent Pendergast</i> series (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/67035.Relic__Pendergast___1_" title="Relic (Pendergast, #1) by Douglas Preston" rel="nofollow noopener">Relic</a>), the <i>Charlie Parker</i> series (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/175242.Every_Dead_Thing__Charlie_Parker___1_" title="Every Dead Thing (Charlie Parker, #1) by John Connolly" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Dead Thing</a>) or the <i>Harry Dresden</i> series (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47212.Storm_Front__The_Dresden_Files___1_" title="Storm Front (The Dresden Files, #1) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Storm Front</a>) would enjoy this, especially considering that <i>The Tomb</i> predates all of these by more than a decade. It <b>is</b> the first novel in a <b>horror / supernatural</b> series, so don’t go into this expecting crime fiction. There <b>will</b> be beasties and there <b>will</b> be blood! blood! blood!<br /><br /><i>…there were rustling and scraping and grunting sounds coming from the darkness beyond that door.</i><br /><br />It’s an enjoyable enough romp with some interesting twists. Some I saw coming. Some I did not. Not too much more I can say about <i>The Tomb</i>. It isn’t subtle and it isn’t fancy, but it gets the job done. I will certainly be reading the other books in this series.<br /><br /><i>She glanced up over the hood and froze in horror at the sight of a dark, dripping, glistening form rising out of the bay.</i><br /><br />Indeed. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4684478014591198518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_571336040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/571336040?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2018-shelf">2018-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer571336040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12399910715184922063">This novel has a lot of modern (80's) thriller sensibilities with a can-do 'fixer' focused mainly on character study and definition, mostly in the same way that horror novels do it. Righting wrongs, giving up close and personal Justice to those who escape the law.<br/><br/>With a supernatural twist. Hindu Rakashas!<br/><br/>It sounds pretty cool, actually, but my personal expectations were more along the lines of a proto-modern UF... and it is. It just happens to be MORE focused on character study and interpersonal</span>
  <span id="freeText12399910715184922063" style="display:none">This novel has a lot of modern (80's) thriller sensibilities with a can-do 'fixer' focused mainly on character study and definition, mostly in the same way that horror novels do it. Righting wrongs, giving up close and personal Justice to those who escape the law.<br /><br />With a supernatural twist. Hindu Rakashas!<br /><br />It sounds pretty cool, actually, but my personal expectations were more along the lines of a proto-modern UF... and it is. It just happens to be MORE focused on character study and interpersonal dynamics. Good for what it is and if you prefer that kind of thing. It's a decent horror, I suppose, but it happens to be perfectly average, as one, unless you give bonus points for using the idea of Rakashas as the primary story.<br /><br />I've read a lot of things like this, however. I enjoyed the exploration of Kali and Hindu mythos well, but I might want to point at Dan Simmon's Song of Kali as a bit more horrific and fascinating.<br /><br />This one, however, is a modern thriller and should have a lot of ongoing appeal. I'll continue the series to see if it continues to evolve. There's a number of books behind this one. :)<br /><br />Final grade? Above average. Solid.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12399910715184922063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1846253209" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1846253209" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1846253209?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1846253209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3079218805132014316">I have a new best friend and his name is Repairman Jack.<br/><br/>With a style reminiscent of Travanian or John D. MacDonald, F. Paul Wilson describes the urban fantasy equivalent of his off the grid anti-hero. Wilson also demonstrates his libertarian values in a protagonist that would make Poul Anderson or Heinlein proud.<br/><br/>While this can be seen as a far-out version of a Travis McGee adventure, urban and contemporary fantasy fans will be drawn to its supernatural qualities. Jack is on the trail of an ancie</span>
  <span id="freeText3079218805132014316" style="display:none">I have a new best friend and his name is Repairman Jack.<br><br>With a style reminiscent of Travanian or John D. MacDonald, F. Paul Wilson describes the urban fantasy equivalent of his off the grid anti-hero. Wilson also demonstrates his libertarian values in a protagonist that would make Poul Anderson or Heinlein proud.<br><br>While this can be seen as a far-out version of a Travis McGee adventure, urban and contemporary fantasy fans will be drawn to its supernatural qualities. Jack is on the trail of an ancient Indian evil that is threatening paying clients, the girl he loves, and his own hide in this very enjoyable 1984 publication that could also be considered in the genres of horror, thriller or science fiction.<br><br>Whatever label a reader chooses, I think we can all agree that this is a fast moving and fun speculative fiction page turner. <br><br>Jack “fixes” things and we’re not talking about electric toasters or smoothie blenders. Jack handles problems related to human interactions. As in the old Goodfellas line, “Hey Vinny, d’you fix that ting?” “Yeah, Paulie, that problem is solved.” But he’s not an organized mobster, he’s an independent contractor. As a matter of fact, in many ways Jack departed from modern day society years ago: he lives outside of civilization but in plain sight, he pays no taxes, deals only in cash, has no legitimate identity besides the succinctly stated, although evasive moniker “Repairman Jack.” Or just Jack.<br><br>Wilson’s prose is clean and fast, this moves like a fast runner, lithe and smooth. I’ll be returning for more fun with Jack. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498703515i/23153798._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="278" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3079218805132014316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3026473461?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ginger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ginger" href="/user/show/14097149-ginger">Ginger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22819874-the-tomb-adversary-cycle-2">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14097149-ginger?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3026473461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1528892388361307065"><b>4.5 stars!</b><br/><br/>This book was fun, super entertaining and easy to read!<br/><br/><b>The Tomb</b> is the first book in the <i>Repairman Jack</i> series. It's got great characters, supernatural elements and the action is fantastic. While reading this, I felt at times that I was eating popcorn and watching an action movie!<br/><br/><b>The Tomb</b> was written back in 1984 so it's got a great 80s feel to the book. It didn't feel dated to me, so kudos to <i>F. Paul Wilson</i> for writing something that can be relatable in 2020.<br/><br/>Jack  is a fixer. He's not</span>
  <span id="freeText1528892388361307065" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars!</b><br /><br />This book was fun, super entertaining and easy to read!<br /><br /><b>The Tomb</b> is the first book in the <i>Repairman Jack</i> series. It's got great characters, supernatural elements and the action is fantastic. While reading this, I felt at times that I was eating popcorn and watching an action movie!<br /><br /><b>The Tomb</b> was written back in 1984 so it's got a great 80s feel to the book. It didn't feel dated to me, so kudos to <i>F. Paul Wilson</i> for writing something that can be relatable in 2020.<br /><br />Jack  is a fixer. He's not a private investigator but he's not a hitman either. He's somewhere in the middle with a strong set of moral codes that he goes by.<br /><br /><b>The Tomb</b> starts off with Jack getting a recommendation from a United Nations diplomat. The man in need is Kusum Bahkti and he's looking for a stolen necklace that was taken from his grandma. Jack takes the case to find the necklace but it only gets more weird, dangerous and complicated from there.<br /><br />If you're a fan of <i>Preston &amp; Child</i> books like the <i>Pendergast</i> series, I think you would really enjoy this series.<br />It's got a strong main character, tons of action and supernatural elements.<br />I really enjoyed <b>The Tomb</b> and can't wait to read more books in this series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1528892388361307065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1347073930" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1347073930" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1347073930?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1347073930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13901112438590005013">Harry Dresden without magic and more violent and more Horror than Urban Fantasy. Repairman Jack takes on jobs that require vigilante justice - "fixing" problems in a way that the usual law enforcement and judiciary can't.<br/><br/>Excellent pacing. Believable(ish) story. Scary monsters. Some genuine suspenseful moments. A step up from book one <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62571.The_Keep__Adversary_Cycle___1_' title='The Keep (Adversary Cycle, #1) by F. Paul Wilson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Keep</a>.<br/><br/>4 Stars<br/><br/>PS: I don't know why this book is called The Tomb - There is no Tomb!</span>
  <span id="freeText13901112438590005013" style="display:none">Harry Dresden without magic and more violent and more Horror than Urban Fantasy. Repairman Jack takes on jobs that require vigilante justice - "fixing" problems in a way that the usual law enforcement and judiciary can't.<br /><br />Excellent pacing. Believable(ish) story. Scary monsters. Some genuine suspenseful moments. A step up from book one <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62571.The_Keep__Adversary_Cycle___1_" title="The Keep (Adversary Cycle, #1) by F. Paul Wilson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Keep</a>.<br /><br />4 Stars<br /><br />PS: I don't know why this book is called The Tomb - There is no Tomb!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13901112438590005013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer17595566331642887595">The only book I have read in the "Repairman Jack" series, and, I think, the last.<br/>Repairman Jack is a below-the-radar fixit guy that "repairs" problems for people. Although he's supposed to be cool and dangerous, he comes across as kind of an idiot man-child to me. He has all these ridiculous methods for keeping his identity secret yet he invites a strange woman up to his apartment early on in the book. He goes to the same bar every single time to interview clients and shops at the same store nea</span>
  <span id="freeText17595566331642887595" style="display:none">The only book I have read in the "Repairman Jack" series, and, I think, the last.<br />Repairman Jack is a below-the-radar fixit guy that "repairs" problems for people. Although he's supposed to be cool and dangerous, he comes across as kind of an idiot man-child to me. He has all these ridiculous methods for keeping his identity secret yet he invites a strange woman up to his apartment early on in the book. He goes to the same bar every single time to interview clients and shops at the same store near his house. (Not exactly below the radar in my book.)Jack watches old movies late into the night in an apartment filled with odd pieces of furniture, old toys and antique kitsch. In the morning he wakes up and eats several bowls of some kind of cold cereal kids eat. Except for the cold blooded killer part he sounds like Tom Hanks' character in "Big."<br />This book is chock full of all the conventional characters--you know, the quirky weapons dealer that can get the hero his flame thrower in the middle of the night, the friendly bar owner that allows Jack to use a private booth for business, the love interest that is repulsed by what Jack does for a living--but just can't keep herself from falling for him...<br />So the only remotely unconventional thing about this book is that it is an odd pairing of mediocre examples of two different genres, the detective/thriller and horror. (Jack has to fight some nearly immortal Indian demons and a one armed disciple of Kali...) <br />Not a good book and I wish I had those hours back...</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_11335525" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11335525" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/316799-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1196198918p2/316799.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11335525?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/316799-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">F. Paul Wilson fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/316799-mark?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11335525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9135405229345297740">"The Tomb", by F. Paul Wilson, is the SECOND book in his "Adversary Cycle" series and the FIRST book in his "Repairman Jack" series.<br/><br/>This novel introduces New Yorker Repairman Jack, a man with no permanent last name (it varies with the ID he's carrying at the time) and no records of his existence (he either had them erased or doesn't reference them at all anymore). His job is to fix things that the police can't or won't fix. Sometimes this involves hurting or killing people, which is why his ex-g</span>
  <span id="freeText9135405229345297740" style="display:none">"The Tomb", by F. Paul Wilson, is the SECOND book in his "Adversary Cycle" series and the FIRST book in his "Repairman Jack" series.<br /><br />This novel introduces New Yorker Repairman Jack, a man with no permanent last name (it varies with the ID he's carrying at the time) and no records of his existence (he either had them erased or doesn't reference them at all anymore). His job is to fix things that the police can't or won't fix. Sometimes this involves hurting or killing people, which is why his ex-girlfriend, Gia, dumped him.<br /><br />I wouldn't think of Repairman Jack as a hired thug or assassin. He's more like "The Equalizer" from that old TV series (only he's not an ex-spy...he has no formal training to speak of). He only kills when there's no other option and he only handles cases that the police can't handle. He does this for money.<br /><br />The Plot<br />Repairman Jack gets two contracts. One from his ex-girlfriend Gia, whose sister-in-law has gone missing and one from an Indian cultural attache' working for the UN, who has lost an important necklace.<br /><br />Of course these two plots intersect and monsters are involved.<br /><br />The Good<br />As a character I liked Repairman Jack. I can definitely see why there's an entire series of books based on him. He's an intriguing character.<br /><br />The book is also well plotted. The pace is just right. Sometimes a novel will conclude and tie up all its loose ends in the last 20 pages. This one is more deliberate in its pacing and it doesn't lag in the middle, like so many of these types of books seem to do.<br /><br />There was a scene in the book where the monsters are holding chunks of bloody flesh that was once human (a character in the book). This scene was genuinely creepy.<br /><br />The main antagonist was a sympathetic one. I like this moral ambiguity in my reads because no one is ALL good or ALL bad.<br /><br />The Bad<br />The characters in the book, besides the protagonist Jack and the main antagonist, are pretty one dimensional. There is a child, Vicky, in the book who is written to be so sweet, she'd turn Satan into a diabetic. Shirley Temple, on her best day, has got nothing on this kid.<br /><br />The monsters were kind of nondescript. I didn't get any real sense of foreboding or threat from them. It seems to me, with a few slight changes, the monsters could be excised from the story entirely and you'd still have the same overall plot.<br /><br />There was also no real connection between this and the previous book, "The Keep", which makes me think that perhaps calling it a part of the "Adversary Cycle" was a way to increase sales. Another reviewer said it was Lovecraftian, but I really didn't get that out of the book at all. There is mention of the "Old Gods" who created the monsters of the book as a "parody of humanity", but that's pretty much it. Even that seemed tacked on as an afterthought and maybe that small fact was the connection between this book and the previous book, "The Keep". I'm not sure.<br /><br />Perhaps I'm not very astute in the literary sense, but I still don't get the title, "The Tomb". To me, "The Necklace" would have been a more apt title.<br /><br />Conclusion<br />It's a good read. Wilson didn't knock the ball out of the park as he did with "The Keep", but it's a book worth reading for the character of Repairman Jack alone. Hopefully the ancillary characters in the Repairman Jack series get more interesting as the series progresses. As far as the "Adversary Cycle" goes, this is a dubious addition to it. I hope that the reason that this book is in the "Adversary Cycle" will become more apparent as I read the later books in the series.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9135405229345297740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_70863811" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70863811" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70863811?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of occult detective novels, kickbutt heroes, and lesser-used folklore elements</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=occult-detective">occult-detective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-to-die-for">hero-to-die-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=tough-as-nails-heroes">tough-as-nails-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=folklore">folklore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70863811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5703376504834506571">I was going to give this three stars, but I realize it deserves more. I think I heard it raved about so much that I expected to like it more. Had I gone into The Tomb with lower expectations, I would have no hesitation in rating it higher. That is why I hate to read books after they are so hyped. It just spoils the experience.<br/><br/>Repairman Jack is just an awesome character. He is a person who exists outside of the system. He simply dropped off the 'grid.' He doesn't pay taxes, and he doesn't feel li</span>
  <span id="freeText5703376504834506571" style="display:none">I was going to give this three stars, but I realize it deserves more. I think I heard it raved about so much that I expected to like it more. Had I gone into The Tomb with lower expectations, I would have no hesitation in rating it higher. That is why I hate to read books after they are so hyped. It just spoils the experience.<br /><br />Repairman Jack is just an awesome character. He is a person who exists outside of the system. He simply dropped off the 'grid.' He doesn't pay taxes, and he doesn't feel like he owes the system anything. That doesn't mean he doesn't have a sense of ethics or morals. He just believes in doing things his way. He is lead by his extremely strong sense of justice, regardless of the cost, because of how his mother was killed. I really admired his character for his ability to be his own person. I think Mr. Wilson did a good job of creating this character. He's a fun guy to follow around as he goes about his work of fixing the unfixable situation. When this story starts, it's clear that supernatural situations aren't really his forte, but after this book, I think Jack will have his feet wet in supernatural matters.<br /><br />I liked the Indian folklore, using the rakoshi, which is an Indian demonic entity that can be called up via a curse. It was funny because I read two books within a short period of time with rakoshi, this and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/837910.Ghosts_of_Albion_Accursed__Ghosts_of_Albion_" title="Ghosts of Albion Accursed (Ghosts of Albion) by Christopher Golden" rel="nofollow noopener">Ghosts of Albion Accursed</a> that incorporated these creatures. I liked that Jack had an Indian love interest, who was easily as complicated as he was. The villain was also conflicted and layered. This story is one in which you can see many sides of the equation, although you know which side you're on, Repairman Jack's. Mr. Wilson really does a great job of showing the backstory to the Indian aspect of this story, heavily tied into the cult of Kali, the destroyer. <br /><br />This is a much an action thriller as it is horror. What a great combination. I love action, and I like a good horror story that relies more on suspense and genuine fear-inspiring storytelling and less on gore. There are a few bloody moments, but this wasn't a gory book, in my opinion. I was glad I read this book, and I do look forward to reading more of Jack's adventures.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5703376504834506571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12024429532695833462">Some years ago I read The Keep. My wife liked it some, I on the other hand wasn't all that impressed. It was the last thing by Mr Wilson I read...till now. A couple of years ago someone suggested to my wife and I that we try the Repairman Jack books, but I never got around to it.<br/><br/>Till now.<br/><br/>I've got to say I liked this book. It's not great literature in the "classic sense" (you may hear that pronounced in a sophisticated accent if you wish). This book started out as what might be called a fairly st</span>
  <span id="freeText12024429532695833462" style="display:none">Some years ago I read The Keep. My wife liked it some, I on the other hand wasn't all that impressed. It was the last thing by Mr Wilson I read...till now. A couple of years ago someone suggested to my wife and I that we try the Repairman Jack books, but I never got around to it.<br /><br />Till now.<br /><br />I've got to say I liked this book. It's not great literature in the "classic sense" (you may hear that pronounced in a sophisticated accent if you wish). This book started out as what might be called a fairly standard thriller and morphed into something like Harry Dresden meets Mitch Rapp. I plan to read the next book.<br /><br />The only odd note? There's no Tomb in the book.<br /><br />It turns out that F. Paul Wilson wanted to title the book Rakoshi (the name of a creature in the book) but the publisher wanted the title to be closer to The Keep. They figured no one would notice there was no tomb in the book. Go figure.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16632266630948685267">I was excited to start this series about this mysterious character Repairman Jack. Jack is a kind man with a little something extra, however, he feels the need to show himself to his family and friends as an underachiever and a bit of a thug. He does this with the hope of hiding his peculiar profession. <br/><br/>When he is asked by an ex girlfriend to help find her missing Aunt he is also contacted by a very strange, foreign man, with deep pockets, who is desperate to have him find a stolen family heirlo</span>
  <span id="freeText16632266630948685267" style="display:none">I was excited to start this series about this mysterious character Repairman Jack. Jack is a kind man with a little something extra, however, he feels the need to show himself to his family and friends as an underachiever and a bit of a thug. He does this with the hope of hiding his peculiar profession. <br /><br />When he is asked by an ex girlfriend to help find her missing Aunt he is also contacted by a very strange, foreign man, with deep pockets, who is desperate to have him find a stolen family heirloom. As the story unfolds he starts to realize that the two cases may be related but has no idea how that could be possible. To protect his ex-girlfriend and her family he must find out more about this odd man, his beautiful sister, why they are in America and what they want.<br /><br />An old curse, things that go bump in the night and a little romance made this an exciting read. There is a book before this one that I will be reading before going on in the series. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chloe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chloe" href="/user/show/70078-chloe">Chloe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780765355133" href="/book/show/219407.The_Tomb_Adversary_Cycle_2_">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chloe by: </span>
      ScottK
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70078-chloe?shelf=not-owned">not-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70078-chloe?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/70078-chloe?shelf=mystery-crime-thriller">mystery-crime-thriller</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70112803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16525952704235568281">Beginning a new series is always a dicey prospect for me. Will it be my kind of series? Will it become my newest temporary addiction, with me scrounging the net to find each and every book in the collection? Will it cause me to begin fantasizing about what it'd be like to exist within that universe? With all these questions rattling about my head, it should be understandable that I was hesitant to begin the Repairman Jack series- especially because I'm loathe to begin a series that has not come </span>
  <span id="freeText16525952704235568281" style="display:none">Beginning a new series is always a dicey prospect for me. Will it be my kind of series? Will it become my newest temporary addiction, with me scrounging the net to find each and every book in the collection? Will it cause me to begin fantasizing about what it'd be like to exist within that universe? With all these questions rattling about my head, it should be understandable that I was hesitant to begin the Repairman Jack series- especially because I'm loathe to begin a series that has not come to an end. Once bitten, twice shy, thank you Robert Jordan.<br /><br />Still, after a friend had touted the glories of the Repairman Jack books to me again and again, I found my curiosity piqued and the walls of my reticence began to crumble. And how fortunate that they did! This book was pure fun from beginning to end. Jack is a great hero- a "repairman" who fixes extralegal problems for his friends and confederates, living off the grid, changing IDs like underwear, endlessly resourceful- he's like MacGuyver but without the jean jacket and the mullet. When you toss in some delightful Indian monsters that are hunting down several of his friends, well you've got the makings of a fast-paced thriller the likes of which I haven't read in a long time.<br /><br />So thank you, Scott, for raising my awareness of these books. I'm firmly hooked now (<i>Legacies</i> is on hold for me at the Library as I type this). Good thing that 13 of the 15 books have been released, because I think I know what I'm going to be doing with my spare reading time this Winter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16525952704235568281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3640145413" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3640145413" />
    <a title="Phil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76396700-phil"><img alt="Phil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516033071p2/76396700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3640145413?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phil" href="/user/show/76396700-phil">Phil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780425072950" href="/book/show/1784493.The_Tomb_Adversary_Cycle_2_">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76396700-phil?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/76396700-phil?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3640145413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8387300644826836455">Another fun read by Wilson! While this is the second in the Adversary Cycle, there is no connection to the first volume (The Keep). Jack the 'repairman' is our main protagonist; a man who keeps off the official radar, with no SSN and about a zillion last names (he goes by Jack). Since his teenage years (we learn as the novel unfolds) Jack 'fixes' things. His first 'fix' involved one of his neighbors. It seems the neighbor loved his lawn, spending endless time manicuring it, etc. Some punks decid</span>
  <span id="freeText8387300644826836455" style="display:none">Another fun read by Wilson! While this is the second in the Adversary Cycle, there is no connection to the first volume (The Keep). Jack the 'repairman' is our main protagonist; a man who keeps off the official radar, with no SSN and about a zillion last names (he goes by Jack). Since his teenage years (we learn as the novel unfolds) Jack 'fixes' things. His first 'fix' involved one of his neighbors. It seems the neighbor loved his lawn, spending endless time manicuring it, etc. Some punks decided to trash the yard for fun, driving their cars on it on night and thoroughly ruining it. So, Jack offered to help. First he planted some yew trees around the edges, and behind them thick pipes filled with cement that only rose a few feet about the ground. Sure enough, the punks waited until the neighbor had re-turfed the yard back to its former splendor and tried to drive on it once again-- big mistake! the cars had their undercarriages ripped out due to the pipes and the drivers and crew sent to the hospital. <br /><br />Move forward a few decades and Jack lives in NYC. This was written in the 1980s, so NYC was still a real city! One day, Jack gets a call (he only works on referrals, in this case, a honcho in the UN) from an Indian guy (a diplomat) whose grandmother was mugged and a necklace stolen. Jack meets the guy and agrees to try to track the mugger down and get the necklace back (the necklace is 'worthless', but a family heirloom). He finds the mugger, gets the necklace back and busts the guys hands badly (fixed). While this is going on, he gets another call. His ex-girlfriend is tight with her former husband's two elderly aunts, and her daughter Vicky likes them as well. It seems, however that one of the aunts disappeared one night without a trace and she wants Jack to help find her. It turns out the Indian guy has some connection to the missing aunt, but exactly what this connection is I will not discuss here due to spoilers. <br /><br />Jack is a fun character, and the slow reveal of his real activities 'fixing things' is a gas. Wilson injects a lot of humor into the story in a snarky way as well. This starts off a bit slow; as in The Keep, Wilson spends some time establishing the characters before the action starts rolling, but once it gets rolling, it really goes! Even though this is a very different book from The Keep, my complaints are largely the same. The female lead once again is a beautiful damsel in distress awaiting rescue and she once again has a romance with the male lead (Jack). If you can get past the gender stereotypes and cheesy romance, you should really enjoy this if you like a horror tale set in a gritty NYC with Eastern mystic overtones. 3.5 stars rounding up!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8387300644826836455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_343336502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/343336502" />
    <a title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog"><img alt="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366465767p2/1059653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/343336502?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog">Kelly H. (Maybedog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-male-protagonist">what-male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-horror">what-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-modern-fantasy">what-modern-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-not-mm">what-not-mm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer343336502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5425649133471386078">3.5 stars but I'm rounding up to 4 because that's what I would have given it if I'd read it with 1984 sensibilities which was when it was published. It was that era when only lip-service was given to equality. It was "accepted" that women were equal and strong and smart but all that meant was having them say a few smart things or show interest in what was going on or just having femal characters. The same went for people of color. We weren't there yet for any other minority groups.<br/><br/>So Wilson's wo</span>
  <span id="freeText5425649133471386078" style="display:none">3.5 stars but I'm rounding up to 4 because that's what I would have given it if I'd read it with 1984 sensibilities which was when it was published. It was that era when only lip-service was given to equality. It was "accepted" that women were equal and strong and smart but all that meant was having them say a few smart things or show interest in what was going on or just having femal characters. The same went for people of color. We weren't there yet for any other minority groups.<br /><br />So Wilson's women are fairly smart, they are strong in that they want to know what's going on, they demand answers, and one tries to find answers for herself. But they aren't really strong in that they don't really do more than talk, their legs turn to rubber or wood when a man is there to do the heavy lifting, and they freeze when things get terrifying (except for one heady moment when one woman actually <i>goes first</i> into a scary passageway, although she does have a magic item that renders her invisible to the bad things she at least went first after panicking and refusing to go for at least a full paragraph!). <br /><br />Later this same woman hears something shocking and is so dazed she needs to be carried, even though Jack is fighting for their lives, terrified by and running from something he knows nothing about and she has known all her life. I actually found the other woman, Gia, a bit more realistic. I completely understood why she left him and why she stayed away despite her love for him. I probably would have done everything I could so he couldn't find me.<br /><br />The writing was smooth, the pacing was good, and the monsters were scary. I really liked Jack. He was fallible. He didn't like to exercise but he forced himself to in order to stay alive. He admitted to himself when he was afraid and when he was in over his head and it was genuine, not a machismo kind of "ah hell, this bugger would make anyone scared" or the fake humility that is also common in urban fantasy. He's also strong and fast like a man of his skills should be. <br /><br />I really liked the subtle emotions, though. I really felt his grief when someone he loved was in danger. I felt his love for the little girl. I felt his confusion and feelings for both women. I really like that he had feelings at all, although he seems very alone to me. Other than Gia, he only has one friend that shows up in the book, a delightful Jewish character himself, and the lone 1980's nod to multiculturalism. I hope Jack is less alone in later books.<br /><br />Other things: I loved the junky home he lives in that everyone else hates; it's so unusual for a character in fiction who's in this kind of role to be tied down with tons of stuff.<br />I hated <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that a woman let's a man go off to rescue her kid without even trying to go with him <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br />I found that some things were told to the reader that should have been immediately obvious to Jack but even after he was almost explicity shown he didn't get: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the chocolates were tainted <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br />It was a little odd that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the creatures could climb down a ramp into the hold when they returned from hunting but couldn't get out on their own <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br />There was a really nice touch at the end <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[where someone turns to look at the bomb but now I can't read my notes. I think it was Jack but why was that special? I don't know. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, it was a solid read that kept me turning the pages and wanting more. Since the sequel was published 14 years later, I'm going to give it a go. If the women are a little less fragile and wimpy I think I'll really love this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5425649133471386078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1307391303" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1307391303" />
    <a title="Seizure Romero" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/293948-seizure-romero"><img alt="Seizure Romero" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331002683p2/293948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1307391303?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seizure Romero" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seizure Romero" href="/user/show/293948-seizure-romero">Seizure Romero</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/293948-seizure-romero?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/293948-seizure-romero?shelf=badassery">badassery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1307391303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7372564884174723384">So... I realize this book was originally published in 1984. It's a little dated. This copy has "Author's Definitive Edition" across the cover and "This revised edition was previously published in 2004 as <i>Rakoshi</i> by Borderlands Press" on the copyright page (this paperback edition was published in 2006). Repairman Jack books have been popping up on my radar for a few years now, and I've been wanting to read the first in the series to see if I want to dive in. I like the premise.<br/><br/>The writing can be.</span>
  <span id="freeText7372564884174723384" style="display:none">So... I realize this book was originally published in 1984. It's a little dated. This copy has "Author's Definitive Edition" across the cover and "This revised edition was previously published in 2004 as <i>Rakoshi</i> by Borderlands Press" on the copyright page (this paperback edition was published in 2006). Repairman Jack books have been popping up on my radar for a few years now, and I've been wanting to read the first in the series to see if I want to dive in. I like the premise.<br /><br />The writing can be... florid at times. Dramatic. This is Wilson's third or fourth book, so I tried to read it in that context as well as in context of the era in which it was published. But when I got to pages 383-4, I read this (Gia is Jack's estranged girlfriend and Vicky is her daughter. Abe is Jack's friend):<br /><br /><blockquote>"No!" Jack's anguished shout was a physical pain in her ear, then he spun away from her, walking a step or two in one direction, then in another, his arms swinging at the air like a windup toy out of control. "He got Vicky! He got Vicky!"<br />"It's all my fault, Jack. If I'd stayed with her instead of watching that stupid movie, Vicky would be all right now."<br />Jack suddenly stopped moving. His arms lay quiet against his sides.<br />"No," he said in a voice that chilled her with its flat, iron tone. "You couldn't have changed the outcome. You'd only be dead."<br />...[a few lines of dialogue w/Abe omitted]<br />Gia stared at Jack as Abe bustled away toward the front of his store. His abrupt change from near hysteria to this cold dispassionate creature before her was almost as terrifying as Vicky's disappearance.<br />"What are you going to do?<br />"I'm going to get her back. And then I'm going to see to it that she is never bothered again."<br />Gia stepped back. For as Jack spoke, he'd turned toward her and looked past her, looked downtown as if seeing through all the buildings between him and whoever was in his thoughts. She let out a small cry when she saw his expression.<br />She was looking at murder... as if Death itself had taken human form. That look on Jack's face--she turned away. She couldn't bear it. More rage and fury than any one man was meant to hold were concentrated in his eyes. She could almost imagine someone's heart stopping just from looking into those eyes.</blockquote><br /><br />I laughed. Out loud. The mood was broken. I finished the book and the end was mildly satisfying, but after that I had a very hard time taking it seriously.<br /><br />Repairman Jack books are now being published in hardback. I've got to believe that Wilson's writing has improved over the years and is much less over-the-top now. What I really don't get, however, is why you would try to update the story for the new century (there are a few added references to modern technology such as IPods, but no cell phones), yet completely fail to remove or rewrite such ridiculous prose (there's quite a bit of it. I just excerpted my favorite). I dunno. I might try a few more books, just to see.<br /><br />Seriously, though....<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7372564884174723384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_70281930" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70281930?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey" href="/user/show/1020736-stacey">Stacey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1020736-stacey?shelf=my-review-or-notes">my-review-or-notes</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70281930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15205832012542517930">A few weeks ago, I was wishing for another pulpy guilty-pleasure series to read; I'm jonesing a bit, since it will be at least 4 more months until the next Dresden fix, heh. One of my IRL friends - the same pusher that hooked me on Dresden - has been trying to get me lit on Repairman Jack. I caved in a moment of weakness.<br/><br/>But... <br/><br/>It's pretty damn good! I saw "series," and assumed "ditch." I forgot that Wilson was already well-established by the time he wrote <i>The Tomb,</i> and that the rest of the seri</span>
  <span id="freeText15205832012542517930" style="display:none">A few weeks ago, I was wishing for another pulpy guilty-pleasure series to read; I'm jonesing a bit, since it will be at least 4 more months until the next Dresden fix, heh. One of my IRL friends - the same pusher that hooked me on Dresden - has been trying to get me lit on Repairman Jack. I caved in a moment of weakness.<br /><br />But... <br /><br />It's pretty damn good! I saw "series," and assumed "ditch." I forgot that Wilson was already well-established by the time he wrote <i>The Tomb,</i> and that the rest of the series was written in response to the success of this novel. And it is pretty damn good. I said that already, I know. I'm just a bit surprised. <br /><br />Jack is an interesting character, his moral compass points in a slightly different direction than most people, but his version of True North is consistent for him. He leads a shadowy life, but believable. If he doesn't use his SS# he doesn't magically get different rules than the rest of Americans, it complicates his life. <br /><br />He has to exercise to stay in shape, that was a nice touch. <br /><br />Damn book cliffhangers though. If I had read this when it came out, I would have been pissed. I hate cliffhangers. Also, I hate pulp series that aren't totally available for my ereader. I had to make an unscheduled run to Powell's for my next 5¢.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3869273901013852805">Cheerful, upbeat sort of horror... Kind of an "Indiana Jones meets the Wolfman" story. Repairman Jack is immediately likable thanks to being introduced in the middle of a James Whale movie festival, and it rolls from there. Ancient Indian monsters are being used by a madman to settle an age-old score, and Jack gets pulled into the middle of it when he's asked to find an old lady's stolen necklace. Daring-do, fisticuffs, and square-jawed heroics ensue. Very enjoyable.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_825547962" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer13742974704078470805">Hmm. I think I would've liked it more if it weren't so dated - this was written in 1984, and while there have been some attempts to modernise it with mentions of Playstation and Grand Theft Auto, the attitudes remind me of Roger Moore era James Bond movies - the hero moves effortlessly between women, sleeping with both and neither seem to mind - indeed both are pretty pathetic. Meanwhile our hero gets himself out of all certain death situations with panache - and gadgets.<br/>So this is the first of </span>
  <span id="freeText13742974704078470805" style="display:none">Hmm. I think I would've liked it more if it weren't so dated - this was written in 1984, and while there have been some attempts to modernise it with mentions of Playstation and Grand Theft Auto, the attitudes remind me of Roger Moore era James Bond movies - the hero moves effortlessly between women, sleeping with both and neither seem to mind - indeed both are pretty pathetic. Meanwhile our hero gets himself out of all certain death situations with panache - and gadgets.<br />So this is the first of the Repairman Jack series, and I probably will continue as it is highly rated, and the later books are a lot more recent so will probably offend me less. Here Jack, a mysterious Mr Fixit who solves people's problems by violent means, is asked by his ex-girlfriend Gia ( who left him because she found out what he did and couldn't handle it, but whose knickers fall off pretty quick as soon as they're alone in a room together) to find her daughter's great-aunt who has mysteriously disappeared from an upstairs bedroom. He is also charged with recovering a necklace stolen from the grandmother of a surly Indian diplomat during a mugging. Can't say much more without spoiling but it all gets silly pdq.<br />I actually do normally like this kind of main character so I expect he'll grow on me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13742974704078470805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_529725745" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/529725745" />
    <a title="S.E." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6181827-s-e"><img alt="S.E." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584603462p2/6181827.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/529725745?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.E." class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.E." href="/user/show/6181827-s-e">S.E.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer529725745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17420860402620665904">Reading this book brings to mind other paranormal series involving male protagonists ie. Jim Butcher’s Harry Dresden series, Kevin Hearne’s Iron Druid Chronicles and Rob Thurman’s Cal & Niko Leandros series. I also couldn’t help but notice that unlike the others who have supernatural powers, Repairman Jack is essentially human, with all the human frailties and limitations. <br/><br/>What Jack lacks in supernatural gifts (found abundantly in Harry Dresden, Cal Leandros and Atticus Sullivan), he’s supposed </span>
  <span id="freeText17420860402620665904" style="display:none">Reading this book brings to mind other paranormal series involving male protagonists ie. Jim Butcher’s Harry Dresden series, Kevin Hearne’s Iron Druid Chronicles and Rob Thurman’s Cal &amp; Niko Leandros series. I also couldn’t help but notice that unlike the others who have supernatural powers, Repairman Jack is essentially human, with all the human frailties and limitations. <br /><br />What Jack lacks in supernatural gifts (found abundantly in Harry Dresden, Cal Leandros and Atticus Sullivan), he’s supposed to make it up with his human power mojo of weapons, fighting skills and wit. That’s well and good, but unfortunately, the full extent and depth of what he's capable of is not sufficiently demonstrated to give his character justice. What I would really like to see is a more convincing display of Jack’s human prowess in getting things done, solving mysteries and fighting his way out of trouble.<br /><br />“The Tomb” is not compulsively readable, but the storyline is engaging enough and I like how the book ended. I would certainly give this series a shot, but I do hope to see its characters grow and become more layered, and of course, witness Jack’s full potential by and by.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17420860402620665904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_384164975" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/384164975" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11382577-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470503541p2/11382577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/384164975?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/11382577-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer384164975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10229100665674487373">This was my first - and THE first - Repairman Jack book, and I really enjoyed it. Well written and super-exciting. <br/><br/>Repairman Jack isn't your average repairman. He doesn't fix appliances or broken fences. He "fixes" things for people who can't, or won't go to the regular authorities for help with problems. Jack is the last resort for people who are desperate for help and have nowhere else to go.<br/><br/>Jack doesn't exist as far as the "normal" world is concerned. He doesn't have a bank account, a social </span>
  <span id="freeText10229100665674487373" style="display:none">This was my first - and THE first - Repairman Jack book, and I really enjoyed it. Well written and super-exciting. <br /><br />Repairman Jack isn't your average repairman. He doesn't fix appliances or broken fences. He "fixes" things for people who can't, or won't go to the regular authorities for help with problems. Jack is the last resort for people who are desperate for help and have nowhere else to go.<br /><br />Jack doesn't exist as far as the "normal" world is concerned. He doesn't have a bank account, a social security number or any legitimate identification, and the IRS doesn't even know he exists. But even so, he's the answer to a prayer for the people who need his help . . . if they can find him, that is.<br /><br />In this book, Jack is approached by a diplomat from India. He tells Jack his grandmother has been mugged and brutally beaten and is at death's door in the hospital. What he asks of Jack is odd, however. One of the things the mugger took is a necklace his grandmother was wearing. He tells Jack the necklace is a family heirloom and of great sentimental value and he wants Jack to find it and return it to her before she dies. And just to make it more complicated he tells Jack he MUST find the necklace and get it back around her neck within 24 hours or she will be dead and it will be too late.<br /><br />Jack takes the assignment, never for a moment believing he has a hope in hell of finding a particular mugger in a city the size of New York, not to mention any hope that the necklace is still in one piece, in 24 hours. And yet, he does!<br /><br />Once the necklace is returned, however, everything gets weird very fast. The grandmother is spirited secretly out of the hospital and the diplomat goes back to his work at the U.N.<br /><br />And Jack goes back to trying to convince his ex-girlfriend Gia to give their relationship another try. When Gia found out what Jack's life is REALLY all about, she could not get past the violence and the secrecy his work involves and she definitely doesn't want him or his work around her young daughter, Vicky. Unfortunately, Vicky adores Jack and can't accept his departure from their lives. So between Jack and Vicky, Gia's having a hard time keeping Jack away, especially since she really loves him.<br /><br />Then, one of Gia's two beloved and elderly aunts by marriage [to her rich but rotten ex-husband now living in London] disappears from their townhouse without a trace. Gia is desperate enough to ask Jack for help finding her.<br /><br />And Jack is happy to help, especially since if he finds Aunt Grace, he hopes Gia will give them another chance. But once he starts investigating, the trail leads back to the Indian diplomat and his younger and beautiful sister. Jack can't figure out what's going on.<br /><br />When he finally does figure out what is happening, he can't believe it. The things he sees and learns can't be real - they just can't! [No spoilers - you'll have to read the book to find out].<br /><br />Things really heat up when Vicky is taken by the same evil that got Aunt Grace. At that point Repairman Jack goes full force and doesn't care who he has to go through to get Vicky back.<br /><br />The story is extremely fast-paced and thrilling. Once the facts about what's going on are revealed, the book moves like lightening and the events really grab you and drag you along with them at 90 miles an hour. Towards the end I realized I was actually holding my breath and that doesn't happen to me very often.<br /><br />There are some aspects of this story that require you to suspend disbelief about what is possible in the real world. But if you can go with Hamlet and embrace his reminder that: "There are more things in heaven and earth, Horatio, than are dreamt of in your philosopy," well then, this is a great thriller with a terrifically exciting plot and great characters. I will definitely read other books in this series and recommend them to others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10229100665674487373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nmPZ2uJV8tT+jXAVqSbKFB0+dos9RD2IS69+qGIMi/L+08g91/rc9IP9aIx9RlvzmD32f++U28bFA6Q3VCLmzw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BhqT6QuIYamW6JICc4mosg4s/zdLoqh/IL5YYssUpxpmqoIOPidPieuYipun6TlViy9/w5lyTjGuEoL9/TrKJw==')})
  }

Women and their deeds are prominent, and freedom (even in sexual matters) is not an invention of the last decades. And when Barzun rates the present not as a culmination but a decline, he is in no way a prophet of doom. Instead, he shows decadence as the creative novelty that will burst forth -- tomorrow or the next day.\n\nOnly after a lifetime of separate studies covering a broad territory could a writer create <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10788629536587995947">Francis Paul Wilson is an author, born in Jersey City, New Jersey. He writes novels and short stories primarily in the science fiction and horror genres. His debut novel was Healer (1976). Wilson is also a part-time practicing family physician. He made his first sales in 1970 to Analog and continued to write science fiction throughout the seventies. In 1981 he ventured into the horror genre with t</span>
  <span id="freeText10788629536587995947" style="display:none">Francis Paul Wilson is an author, born in Jersey City, New Jersey. He writes novels and short stories primarily in the science fiction and horror genres. His debut novel was Healer (1976). Wilson is also a part-time practicing family physician. He made his first sales in 1970 to Analog and continued to write science fiction throughout the seventies. In 1981 he ventured into the horror genre with the international bestseller, The Keep, and helped define the field throughout the rest of the decade. In the 1990s he became a true genre hopper, moving from science fiction to horror to medical thrillers and branching into interactive scripting for Disney Interactive and other multimedia companies. He, along with Matthew J. Costello, created and scripted FTL Newsfeed which ran daily on the Sci-Fi Channel from 1992-1996.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/fpaulwilson">http://us.macmillan.com/author/fpaulw...</a></span>
